## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics (classical mechanics)
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration typically involves nonlinear restoring forces (polynomial in x), possibly nonlinear damping (functions of v), and potentially time-dependent driving forces.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (periodic driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (c2 + c3 * x**2) (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring)
- Quadratic-cubic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric potential)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 + c2 * v (position-dependent damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)
- Combined nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 (nonlinear restoring + nonlinear damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = x * (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (quadratic nonlinearity with damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential well; even powers (x²) → asymmetric potential
- Position-dependent damping terms like v*x² indicate energy exchange that depends on amplitude (van der Pol type)
- Cubic restoring force x³ with same sign as linear term x → hardening spring; opposite sign → softening spring
- Velocity terms proportional to v indicate energy dissipation/injection; absence of v terms implies conservative system
- Explicit time dependence through trigonometric functions cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) indicates external periodic driving
- Products of v and powers of x (e.g., v*x², v*x⁴) represent nonlinear damping where dissipation depends on displacement
- Odd powers of velocity (v³, v⁵) preserve time-reversal antisymmetry of damping; even powers (v²) break it
- Absence of explicit time dependence t suggests an autonomous system where phase-space analysis suffices
